class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Union Jack</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Flag&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a>)</span></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Union Flag" redirects here. For other uses of Union Flag, see <a href="/wiki/Union_flag_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Union flag (disambiguation)">Union flag (disambiguation)</a>. For other uses of Union Jack, see <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Union Jack (disambiguation)">Union Jack (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption>Union Jack</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;display:none">\n</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image" title="The Union Flag: a red cross over combined red and white saltires, all with white borders, over a dark blue background."><img alt="The Union Flag: a red cross over combined red and white saltires, all with white borders, over a dark blue background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/255px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="255" height="128" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/383px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/510px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/List_of_flag_names" title="List of flag names">Names</a></th><td>\nUnion Flag, Union Jack, Royal Union Flag</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_vexillology" title="Glossary of vexillology">Use</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/National_flag" title="National flag">National flag</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Proportion</th><td>\n1:2</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Adopted</th><td>\n1801</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Design</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Scotland" title="Flag of Scotland">Cross of Saint Andrew</a> <a href="/wiki/Counterchanged" class="mw-redirect" title="Counterchanged">counterchanged</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_Saint_Patrick" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross of Saint Patrick">Cross of Saint Patrick</a>, over all the <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Cross">Cross of Saint George</a>.</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Union Jack</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> or <b>Union Flag</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Flag of the United Kingdom">national flag of the United Kingdom</a>. The flag also has an official or semi-official status in some other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>: for example, it is a ceremonial flag in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> by parliamentary resolution, and known there as the <b>Royal Union Flag</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-ruf_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ruf-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Further, it is used as an official flag in some of the smaller <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territories">British overseas territories</a>. The Union Flag also appears in the <a href="/wiki/Flag_terminology#Flag_elements" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag terminology">canton</a> (upper left-hand quarter) of the flags of several nations and territories that are former British possessions or <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">dominions</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Hawaii" title="Flag of Hawaii">state flag of Hawaii</a>.\n</p><p>The claim that the term <i>Union Jack</i> properly refers only to naval usage has been disputed, following historical investigations by the <a href="/wiki/Flag_Institute" title="Flag Institute">Flag Institute</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The origins of the earlier <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Great_Britain" title="Flag of Great Britain">flag of Great Britain</a> date back to 1606. <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI of Scotland</a> had inherited the English and Irish thrones in 1603 as James I, thereby <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Crowns" title="Union of the Crowns">uniting the crowns</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Scotland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Ireland</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a>, although the three kingdoms remained separate states. On 12 April 1606, a new flag to represent this regal union between England and Scotland was specified in a royal decree, according to which the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_England" title="Flag of England">flag of England</a> (a red cross on a white background, known as <i><a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Cross">St George\'s Cross</a></i>), and the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Scotland" title="Flag of Scotland">flag of Scotland</a> (a white <a href="/wiki/Saltire" title="Saltire">saltire</a> on a blue background, known as the <i>Saltire</i> or <i>St Andrew\'s Cross</i>), would be joined together, forming the flag of England and Scotland for maritime purposes. King James also began to refer to a "Kingdom of Great Britaine", although the union remained a personal one.\n</p><p>The present design of the Union Flag dates from a Royal proclamation following the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1800" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Union 1800">union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Ireland</a> in 1801.<sup id="cite_ref-flaginst_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flaginst-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The flag combines aspects of three older national flags: the red cross of <a href="/wiki/St_George" class="mw-redirect" title="St George">St George</a> for the Kingdom of England, the white saltire of <a href="/wiki/St_Andrew" class="mw-redirect" title="St Andrew">St Andrew</a> for <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> (which two were united in the first Union Flag), and the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Saltire" title="Saint Patrick&#39;s Saltire">red saltire</a> of <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick" class="mw-redirect" title="St Patrick">St Patrick</a> to represent <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>.\n</p><p>Notably, the <a href="/wiki/Home_Nations" title="Home Nations">home country</a> of <a href="/wiki/Symbols_of_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Symbols of Wales">Wales is not represented separately</a> in the Union Flag, as the flag was designed after the invasion of Wales in 1282. Hence Wales as a home country today has no representation on the flag; it appears under the cross of St George, which represents the former Kingdom of England (<a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">which included Wales</a>).\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Union_Flag_and_St_Georges_Cross.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Union_Flag_and_St_Georges_Cross.jpg/220px-Union_Flag_and_St_Georges_Cross.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Union_Flag_and_St_Georges_Cross.jpg/440px-Union_Flag_and_St_Georges_Cross.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1356" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Union_Flag_and_St_Georges_Cross.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Union Jack flying beside Saint George\'s Cross</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg/220px-HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg/330px-HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg/440px-HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="686" data-file-height="528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Cornwall_F99_July_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Cornwall_(F99)" title="HMS Cornwall (F99)">HMS&#160;<i>Cornwall</i></a>, "dressed" on the occasion of her official visit to the port of <a href="/wiki/Zeebrugge" title="Zeebrugge">Zeebrugge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, in 2006, and flying the Union Jack from the jackstaff.</div></div></div>\n<p>The terms <i>Union Jack</i> and <i>Union Flag</i> are both historically correct for describing the <i>de facto</i> national flag of the United Kingdom. Whether the term <i>Union Jack</i> applies only when used as a <a href="/wiki/Jack_(flag)" title="Jack (flag)">jack</a> flag on a ship is a modern matter of debate.<sup id="cite_ref-FlagInstitute_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FlagInstitute-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> "Until the early 17th century England and Scotland were two entirely independent kingdoms. This changed dramatically in 1603 on the death of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a>. Because the Queen died unmarried and childless, the English crown passed to the next available heir, her cousin James VI, King of Scotland.  England and Scotland now shared the same monarch under what was known as a union of the crowns.\n</p><p>In 1606, James VI gave orders for a British flag to be created which bore the combined crosses of St. George and of St. Andrew.  The result was the Union Jack.\n</p><p>\nAccording to the <a href="/wiki/Flag_Institute" title="Flag Institute">Flag Institute</a>, a membership-run <a href="/wiki/Vexillological" class="mw-redirect" title="Vexillological">vexillological</a> charity,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> "the national flag of the United Kingdom, the Crown Dependencies and Overseas Territories is the Union Flag, which may also be called the Union Jack."<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The institute also notes: </p><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>it is often stated that the Union Flag should only be described as the Union Jack when flown in the bows of a warship, but this is a relatively recent idea. From early in its life the Admiralty itself frequently referred to the flag as the Union Jack, whatever its use, and in 1902 an Admiralty circular announced that Their Lordships had decided that either name could be used officially. In 1908, a government minister stated, in response to a parliamentary question, that "the Union Jack should be regarded as the National flag".<sup id="cite_ref-FlagInstitute_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FlagInstitute-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote><p> Notwithstanding Their Lordships\' circular of 1902, by 1913 the Admiralty described the "Union Flag" and added in a foot note that \'A Jack is a Flag to be flown only on the "Jack" Staff\'.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, the authoritative <i>A Complete Guide to Heraldry</i> published in 1909 by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Charles_Fox-Davies" title="Arthur Charles Fox-Davies">Arthur Charles Fox-Davies</a> uses the term "Union Jack".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The term "Union Flag" is used in <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">King Charles I\'s</a> 1634 proclamation:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>... none of Our Subjects, of any of Our Nations and Kingdoms shall from henceforth presume to carry the Union Flag in the Main top, or other part of any of their Ships (that is) St Georges cross and St Andrew\'s Cross joined together upon pain of Our high displeasure, but that the same Union Flag be still reserved as an ornament proper for Our own Ships and Ships in our immediate Service and Pay, and none other."<sup id="cite_ref-Perrin_59_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perrin_59-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Proclamation appointing the Flag, as well for Our Navy Royal as for the Ships of Our Subjects of South and North Britain&#160;&#8211;&#32;5 May 1634</cite></div>\n</blockquote><p> and in <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a>\'s proclamation of 1 January 1801 concerning the arms and flag of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland:\n</p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>And that the Union Flag shall be Azure, the Crosses Saltires of St. Andrew and St. Patrick Quarterly per Saltire, counterchanged Argent and Gules; the latter fimbriated of the Second, surmounted by the Cross of St. George of the Third, fimbriated as the Saltire&#160;: ...<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>A Proclamation Declaring His Majesty\'s Pleasure concerning the Royal Style and Titles appertaining to the Imperial Crown of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland, and its Dependencies, and also the Ensigns, Armorial Flags, and Banners thereof"</cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif" class="image"><img alt="The development of The Union Jack (GIF)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif/220px-Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif/330px-Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif/440px-Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Development_of_The_Union_Jack.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The development of The Union Jack.</div></div></div>\n<p>When the first flag representing Britain was introduced on the <a href="/wiki/Proclamation" title="Proclamation">proclamation</a> of <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="James I of England">King James I</a> in 1606,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> it became known simply as the "British flag" or the "flag of Britain". The royal proclamation gave no distinctive name to the new flag. The word "jack" was in use before 1600 to describe the <a href="/wiki/Jack_(flag)" title="Jack (flag)">maritime bow flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FlagInstitute_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FlagInstitute-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> By 1627 a small Union Jack was commonly flown in this position. One theory goes that for some years it would have been called just the "Jack", or "Jack flag", or the "King\'s Jack", but by 1674, while formally referred to as "His Majesty\'s Jack", it was commonly called the "Union Jack", and this was officially acknowledged.<sup id="cite_ref-flaginst_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flaginst-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Amongst the proclamations issued by King George III at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1800" title="Acts of Union 1800">Union</a> of 1801 was a proclamation concerning flags at sea, which repeatedly referred to "Ensigns, Flags, Jacks, and Pendants" and forbade merchant vessels from wearing "Our Jack, commonly called the Union Jack" nor any pendants or colours used by the King\'s ships.<sup id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_1801-01-03_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_1801-01-03-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  Reinforcing the distinction the King\'s proclamation of the same day concerning the arms and flag of the United Kingdom (not colours at sea) called the new flag "the Union Flag".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The size and power of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> internationally at the time could also explain why the flag was named the "Union Jack"; considering the navy was so widely utilised and renowned by the United Kingdom and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">colonies</a>, it is possible that the term <i>jack</i> occurred because of its regular use on all British ships using the jack staff (a flag pole attached to the bow of a ship). The term <i>Union Jack</i> possibly dates from Queen Anne\'s time (r. 1702\xe2\x80\x9314), but its origin is uncertain. It may come from the \'jack-et\' of the English or Scottish soldiers, or from the name of James I who originated the first union in 1603. Even if the term "Union Jack" does derive from the jack flag, after three centuries, it is now sanctioned by use and has appeared in official use, confirmed as the national flag by Parliament and remains the popular term.<sup id="cite_ref-Flagsofworld_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flagsofworld-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winston Churchill was Prime Minister of the United Kingdom from 1940 to 1945 and he referred to the flag of the United Kingdom as the Union Jack. In March 1899 Churchill wrote to his mother from India about her plans to produce a new trans-Atlantic magazine, to be called <i>The Anglo-Saxon Review</i>. The drawing at the end of this letter was deliberately mischievous, teasing her for going down-market, and in the accompanying letter he wrote, "Your title \'The Anglo Saxon\' with its motto \'Blood is thicker than water\' only needs the Union Jack &amp; the Star Spangled Banner crossed on the cover to be suited to one of Harmsworth\xe2\x80\x99s [a leading British newspaper owner] cheap Imperialist productions."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles"><span title="The paragraph near this tag may contain information that is not relevant to the article&#39;s main topic. (August 2016)">relevant?</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:Union_Jack#Churchill_on_the_flag" title="Talk:Union Jack">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>More recently, Reed\'s <i>Nautical Almanac</i> (1990 edition) unambiguously stated: "The Union Flag, frequently but incorrectly referred to as the Union Jack, ..." and later: "8. <b>The Jack</b> \xe2\x80\x93 A small flag worn on a jackstaff on the stem of Naval Vessels.  The Royal Navy wears the Union Flag ... This is the only occasion when it correct to describe the flag as the Union Jack".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> However, this assertion does not appear in any Reed\'s <i>Nautical Almanac</i> since 1993.  In  the 2016 Reeds Nautical Almanac  the only entry where this might appear, section 5.21, covering Flag Etiquette,  does not include this statement. Within the Almanac, neither the Union Flag or the Union Jack are  included  pictorially or mentioned by name.\n</p><p>For comparison with another anglophone country with a large navy: the <a href="/wiki/Jack_of_the_United_States" title="Jack of the United States">Jack of the United States</a> specifically refers to the flag flown from the jackstaff of a warship, auxiliary or other U.S. governmental entity.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The current flag\'s design has been in use since 1801.  Its original <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazon</a>, as decreed by <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">George III of the United Kingdom</a> on 1 January 1801, reads: \n</p>\n<dl><dd>"the Union flag shall be azure, the crosses-saltires of St. Andrew and St. Patrick quartered per saltire <a href="/wiki/Counterchanged" class="mw-redirect" title="Counterchanged">counter changed</a> argent and gules; the latter fimbriated of the second  [viz., argent]; surmounted by the cross of St. George of the third [viz., gules], fimbriated as the saltire [viz., argent]."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specification">Specification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Specification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_Flag_Specifications.svg" class="image" title="Diagram of the Union Flag&#39;s design"><img alt="Diagram of the Union Flag&#39;s design" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Kingdom_Flag_Specifications.svg/350px-United_Kingdom_Flag_Specifications.svg.png" width="350" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Kingdom_Flag_Specifications.svg/525px-United_Kingdom_Flag_Specifications.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Kingdom_Flag_Specifications.svg/700px-United_Kingdom_Flag_Specifications.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="370" /></a></div>\n<p>The Union Jack is normally twice as long as it is tall, a ratio of 1:2. In the United Kingdom, land flags are normally a ratio of 3:5; the Union Jack can also be made in this shape, but is 1:2 for most purposes. In 2008, MP <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Rosindell" title="Andrew Rosindell">Andrew Rosindell</a> proposed a <a href="/wiki/Ten_Minute_Rule" title="Ten Minute Rule">Ten Minute Rule</a> bill to standardise the design of the flag at 3:5, but the bill did not proceed past the first reading.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Flags that have the Union Jack in the canton should always be 1:2 to preserve the square fly area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The three component crosses that make up the Union Flag are sized as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The red <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Cross">St George\'s Cross</a> width is &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>5</sub></span> of the flag\'s height with a &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>15</sub></span> flag height <a href="/wiki/Fimbriation" title="Fimbriation">fimbriation</a></li>\n<li>The white diagonal <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Scotland" title="Flag of Scotland">St Andrew\'s Cross</a> width is &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>6</sup>&#8260;<sub>30</sub></span> of the flag\'s height, visible on either side of the St Patrick\'s Cross in diagonals of  &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>10</sub></span> and &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>30</sub></span> of the flag\'s height, respectively.</li>\n<li>The red diagonal <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Saltire" title="Saint Patrick&#39;s Saltire">St Patrick\'s Cross</a> width is &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>15</sub></span> of the flag\'s height. It is offset by  &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>30</sub></span> of the flag\'s height in anti-clockwise direction. According to the official blazon of 1801, the white diagonal <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Scotland" title="Flag of Scotland">St Andrew\'s Cross</a> is in fact <a href="/wiki/Counterchanged" class="mw-redirect" title="Counterchanged">counterchanged</a> with the red diagonal of  <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Saltire" title="Saint Patrick&#39;s Saltire">St Patrick\'s Cross</a>. In this interpretation, the width of both saltires is  &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>15</sub></span> of the flag\'s height, with fimbriations of  &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>30</sub></span> of the flag\'s height on either side of the red saltire.</li></ul>\n<p>The crosses and fimbriations retain their thickness relative to the flag\'s <i>height</i> whether they are shown with a ratio of 3:5 or 1:2\n</p><p>The Admiralty in 1864 settled all official flags at proportions 1:2, but the relative widths of the crosses remained unspecified, with the above conventions becoming standardised in the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\nIn the 19th century, the Union flag was defined by the same blazon but could vary in its geometrical proportions,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours">Colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The colour specifications for the colours Union Jack (royal) blue, Union Flag red and white are:<sup id="cite_ref-Flagsofworld_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flagsofworld-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Scheme\n</th>\n<th style="background:#012169; color:white;">Blue<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th style="background:#C8102E; color:white;">Red<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th style="background:white; color:black;">White\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a> (paper)\n</th>\n<td>280 C\n</td>\n<td>186 C\n</td>\n<td>Safe\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Web_colors" title="Web colors">HEX</a>\n</th>\n<td>#012169\n</td>\n<td>#C8102E\n</td>\n<td>#FFFFFF\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">MoD</a>\n</th>\n<td>8711D\n</td>\n<td>8711\n</td>\n<td>8711J\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/NATO_Stock_Number" title="NATO Stock Number">NSN</a>\n</th>\n<td>8305.99.130.4580\n</td>\n<td>8305.99.130.4584\n</td>\n<td>8305.99.130.4585\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a>\n</th>\n<td>100.85.5.22\n</td>\n<td>2.100.85.6\n</td>\n<td>0.0.0.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/RGB_color_model" title="RGB color model">RGB</a>\n</th>\n<td>1, 33, 105\n</td>\n<td>200, 16, 46\n</td>\n<td>255, 255, 255\n</td></tr></tbody></table><p>All <a href="/wiki/Web_colors" title="Web colors">HEX</a>, <a href="/wiki/CMYK_color_model" title="CMYK color model">CMYK</a> and <a href="/wiki/RGB_color_model" title="RGB color model">RGB</a> specifications for the <a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a> colours are taken from the official Pantone website on the webpages of the corresponding colours. Keep in mind that although the colour schemes are official, not all of the colours are completely congruent. This is due to different specifications for different types of media (for example, screen and print).\n</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flying">Flying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flying">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><center>Hoist on the right</center></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent"><i>Correct</i> way to fly the flag</div></div></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_(hoist_left).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_left%29.svg/150px-Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_left%29.svg.png" width="150" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_left%29.svg/225px-Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_left%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_left%29.svg/300px-Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_left%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="374" data-file-height="224" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><center>Hoist on the left</center></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_(hoist_right).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_right%29.svg/150px-Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_right%29.svg.png" width="150" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_right%29.svg/225px-Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_right%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_right%29.svg/300px-Upside_down_Union_Flag_on_staff_%28hoist_right%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="374" data-file-height="224" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><center>Hoist on the right</center></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent"><i>Incorrect</i> way to fly the flag</div></div></div>\n<p>The flag does not have reflection symmetry due to the slight pinwheeling of the St Patrick\'s and St Andrew\'s crosses, technically the <i><a href="/wiki/Counterchanged" class="mw-redirect" title="Counterchanged">counterchange</a> of saltires</i>. Thus, there is a right side up.  The original specification of the Union Flag in the Royal Proclamation of 1 January 1801 did not contain a drawn pattern or express which way the saltires should lie; they were simply "counterchanged" and the red saltire fimbriated. Nevertheless, a convention was soon established which accords most closely with the description.\n</p><p>When statically displayed, the hoist is on the observer\'s left. To fly the flag correctly, the white of St Andrew is <i>above</i> the red of St Patrick in the upper hoist canton (the quarter at the top nearest to the flag-pole). This is expressed by the phrases <i>wide white top</i> and <i>broad side up</i>.\n</p><p>The first drawn pattern for the flag was in a parallel proclamation on 1 January 1801, concerning civil naval ensigns, which drawing shows the <a href="/wiki/Red_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="Red ensign">red ensign</a> (also to be used as a red jack by <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a>).  As it appears in the <i><a href="/wiki/London_Gazette" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gazette">London Gazette</a></i>, the broad stripe is where expected for three of the four quarters, but the upper left quarter shows the broad stripe below.<sup id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_1801-01-03_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_1801-01-03-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is often stated that a flag upside down is a form of distress signal or even a deliberate insult. In the case of the Union Flag, the difference is subtle and is easily missed by the uninformed. It is often displayed upside down inadvertently\xe2\x80\x94even on commercially-made hand waving flags.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 February 2009, the BBC reported that the flag had been inadvertently flown upside-down by the UK government at the signing of a trade agreement with Chinese premier <a href="/wiki/Wen_Jiabao" title="Wen Jiabao">Wen Jiabao</a>. The error had been spotted by readers of the BBC news website who had contacted the BBC after seeing a photograph of the event.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5232" data-file-height="3154" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willem_van_der_Stoop_-_The_Battle_of_Chatham_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Raid_on_the_Medway" title="Raid on the Medway">Attack on the Medway</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a>, June 1667</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1603, <a href="/wiki/James_VI_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="James VI of Scotland">James VI of Scotland</a> inherited the English and Irish thrones (as James I), thereby <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Crowns" title="Union of the Crowns">uniting the crowns</a> of England, Scotland and Ireland (which remained separate states) in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Flagsofworld_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flagsofworld-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On 12 April 1606, a new flag to represent this regal union between England and Scotland was specified in a royal decree, according to which the flag of England (a red cross on a white background, known as St George\'s Cross), and the flag of Scotland (a white saltire on a blue background, known as the saltire or St Andrew\'s Cross), would be joined together,<sup id="cite_ref-flaginst_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flaginst-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> forming the flag of Great Britain and first union flag:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>By the King: Whereas, some differences hath arisen between Our subjects of South and North Britaine travelling by Seas, about the bearing of their Flagges: For the avoiding of all contentions hereafter. We have, with the advice of our Council, ordered: That from henceforth all our Subjects of this Isle and Kingdome of Great Britaine, and all our members thereof, shall beare in their main-toppe the Red Crosse, commonly called St George\'s Crosse, and the White Crosse, commonly called St Andrew\xe2\x80\x99s Crosse, joyned together according to the forme made by our heralds, and sent by Us to our Admerall to be published to our Subjects: and in their fore-toppe our Subjects of South Britaine shall weare the Red Crosse onely as they were wont, and our Subjects of North Britaine in their fore-toppe the White Crosse onely as they were accustomed.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption>Great Britain</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;display:none">\n</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Great_Britain_(1707%E2%80%931800).svg" class="image" title="Red cross with white border over a white saltire and dark blue background."><img alt="Red cross with white border over a white saltire and dark blue background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg/255px-Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg.png" width="255" height="153" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg/383px-Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg/510px-Flag_of_Great_Britain_%281707%E2%80%931800%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/List_of_flag_names" title="List of flag names">Name</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Great_Britain" title="Flag of Great Britain">The King\'s Colours or Great Union Flag</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_vexillology" title="Glossary of vexillology">Use</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/National_flag" title="National flag">National flag</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Proportion</th><td>\n3:5</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Adopted</th><td>\n1606\xe2\x80\x931707 (ships at sea), 1707\xe2\x80\x931801 (England and Scotland)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Relinquished</th><td>\n1801</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Design</th><td>\nThe Cross of St George over the Cross of St Andrew</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>This royal flag was, at first, to be used only at sea on civil and military ships of both England and Scotland, whereas land forces continued to use their respective national banners.<sup id="cite_ref-KnowBritain_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KnowBritain-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 1634, <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">King Charles I</a> restricted its use to the royal ships.<sup id="cite_ref-Perrin_59_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perrin_59-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a>, the flag gained a regularised status as "the ensign armorial of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>", the newly created state. It was then adopted by land forces as well, although the blue field used on land-based versions more closely resembled that of the blue of the flag of Scotland.\n</p><p>Various shades of blue have been used in the saltire over the years. The ground of the current Union Flag is a deep "<a href="/wiki/Navy_blue" title="Navy blue">navy</a>" blue (<a href="/wiki/Pantone" title="Pantone">Pantone</a> 280), which can be traced to the colour used for the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ensign" title="Blue Ensign">Blue Ensign</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>\'s historic "Blue Squadron". (Dark shades of colour were used on <a href="/wiki/Maritime_flags" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime flags">maritime flags</a> on the basis of durability.) In 2003 a committee of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> recommended that the flag of Scotland use a lighter "<a href="/wiki/Royal_blue" title="Royal blue">royal</a>" blue, (Pantone 300). (The Office of the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lyon" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Lyon">Lord Lyon</a> does not detail specific shades of colour for use in heraldry.)\n</p><p>A thin white stripe, or <a href="/wiki/Fimbriation" title="Fimbriation">fimbriation</a>, separates the red cross from the blue field, in accordance with heraldry\'s <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_tincture" title="Rule of tincture">rule of tincture</a> where colours (like red and blue) must be separated from each other by metals (like white, i.e. <i><a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">argent</a></i> or silver). The <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazon</a> for the old union flag, to be compared with the current flag, is <i>azure, the cross saltire of St Andrew argent surmounted by the Cross of St George gules, fimbriated of the second.</i>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> had no explicit recognition in the Union Jack as it had been a part of the Kingdom of England since being annexed by <a href="/wiki/Edward_I_of_England" title="Edward I of England">Edward I of England</a> in 1282 and its full integration by the <a href="/wiki/Laws_in_Wales_Acts_1535%E2%80%931542" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws in Wales Acts 1535\xe2\x80\x931542">Laws in Wales Acts 1535\xe2\x80\x931542</a>, and was therefore represented by the flag of England.<sup id="cite_ref-KnowBritain_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KnowBritain-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_(1658-1660).svg" class="image"><img alt="Red cross with white border over a white saltire and dark blue background. At the centre is a gold harp in dark blue shield, which is the same size as the intersection of vertical and horizontal white bars." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_%281658-1660%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_%281658-1660%29.svg.png" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_%281658-1660%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_%281658-1660%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_%281658-1660%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_%281658-1660%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Commonwealth_(1658-1660).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Protectorate_Jack" class="mw-redirect" title="Protectorate Jack">Protectorate Jack</a>, 1658\xe2\x80\x9360</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a>, which had existed as a personal union with England since 1541, was likewise unrepresented in the original versions of the Union Jack.<sup id="cite_ref-KnowBritain_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KnowBritain-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> However, the flag of <a href="/wiki/The_Protectorate" title="The Protectorate">the Protectorate</a> from 1658 to 1660 was <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">inescutcheoned</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Arms_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Arms of Ireland">arms of Ireland</a>. These were removed at <a href="/wiki/English_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="English Restoration">the Restoration</a>, because <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> disliked them.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The original flag appears in the canton of the Commissioners\' Ensign of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Lighthouse_Board" title="Northern Lighthouse Board">Northern Lighthouse Board</a>. This is the only contemporary official representation of the pre-1801 Union Jack in the United Kingdom<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and can be seen flying from their <a href="/wiki/George_Street,_Edinburgh" title="George Street, Edinburgh">George Street</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.\n</p><p>This version of the Union Jack is also shown in the <a href="/wiki/Canton_(flag)" title="Canton (flag)">canton</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Union_Flag" title="Grand Union Flag">Grand Union Flag</a> (also known as the Congress Flag, the First Navy Ensign, the Cambridge Flag and the Continental Colours), the first widely used <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States" title="Flag of the United States">flag of the United States</a>, slowly phased out after 1777.\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Lord_Howe%27s_action,_or_the_Glorious_First_of_June" title="Lord Howe&#39;s action, or the Glorious First of June">Lord Howe\'s action, or the Glorious First of June</a></i>, painted in 1795, shows a Union flying from <a href="/wiki/HMS_Queen_Charlotte_(1790)" title="HMS Queen Charlotte (1790)">HMS&#160;<i>Queen Charlotte</i></a> on the "<a href="/wiki/Glorious_First_of_June" title="Glorious First of June">Glorious First of June</a>" 1794. The actual flag, preserved in the <a href="/wiki/National_Maritime_Museum" title="National Maritime Museum">National Maritime Museum</a>, is a cruder approximation of the proper specifications; this was common in 18th and early 19th century flags.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The flag is also flown beside <a href="/wiki/Customs_House,_Sydney" title="Customs House, Sydney">Customs House</a> in Loftus Street, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, to mark the approximate location at which <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Phillip" title="Arthur Phillip">Captain Phillip</a> first raised the Union Jack, and claimed <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> in 1788. On the plaque it is referred to as the "Jack of Queen Anne".\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>\'s flag is the Union Jack, but in 1938, a "British Army Non-Ceremonial Flag" was devised, featuring a lion on crossed blades with the <a href="/wiki/St_Edward%27s_Crown" title="St Edward&#39;s Crown">St Edward\'s Crown</a> on a red background. This is not the equivalent of the ensigns of the other armed services, but is used at recruiting and military or sporting events, when the army needs to be identified but the reverence and ceremony due to the <a href="/wiki/Regiment" title="Regiment">regimental</a> flags and the Union Jack would be inappropriate.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_proposed_versions">Other proposed versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other proposed versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss,_c.1617.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss%2C_c.1617.JPG/120px-Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss%2C_c.1617.JPG" width="120" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss%2C_c.1617.JPG/180px-Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss%2C_c.1617.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss%2C_c.1617.JPG/240px-Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss%2C_c.1617.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2161" data-file-height="1840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Linlithgow_Palace_unicorn_boss,_c.1617.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Linlithgow Palace carving, c.1617</div></div></div>\n<p>Various other designs for a common flag were drawn up following the union of the two Crowns in 1603, but were rarely, if ever, used.<sup id="cite_ref-plantagenet_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plantagenet-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> One version showed St George\'s cross with St Andrew\'s cross in the canton, and another version placed the two crosses side by side. A painted wooden ceiling boss from <a href="/wiki/Linlithgow_Palace" title="Linlithgow Palace">Linlithgow Palace</a>, dated to about 1617, depicts the Scottish royal unicorn holding a flag where a blue <a href="/wiki/Saltire" title="Saltire">Saltire</a> surmounts the red cross of St. George.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_Union_Flag">Scottish Union Flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Scottish Union Flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg" class="image"><img alt="White saltire clearly visible over white-bordered red cross on blue background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg/220px-Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg.png" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg/330px-Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg/440px-Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Union_Jack_1606_Scotland.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Unofficial Scottish Union Flag</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BeaumontScottishUnionFlag.png" class="image"><img alt="White saltire clearly visible over white-bordered red cross on blue background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/BeaumontScottishUnionFlag.png/220px-BeaumontScottishUnionFlag.png" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d4/BeaumontScottishUnionFlag.png 1.5x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BeaumontScottishUnionFlag.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Unofficial Scottish Union Flag in the 1704 edition of <i>The Present State of the Universe</i></div></div></div>\n<p>In objecting to the design of Union Flag adopted in 1606, whereby the cross of Saint George surmounted that of Saint Andrew, a group of Scots took up the matter with <a href="/wiki/John_Erskine,_18th_Earl_of_Mar" class="mw-redirect" title="John Erskine, 18th Earl of Mar">John Erskine, 18th Earl of Mar</a>, and were encouraged by him to send a letter of complaint to James VI, via the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Scotland" title="Privy Council of Scotland">Privy Council of Scotland</a>, which stated that the flag\'s design "<i>will breid some heit and miscontentment betwix your Majesties subjectis, and it is to be feirit that some inconvenientis sail fall oute betwix thame, for our seyfaring men cannot be inducit to resave that flage as it is set down</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Although documents accompanying this complaint which contained drafts for alternative designs have been lost, evidence exists, at least on paper, of an unofficial Scottish variant, whereby the Scottish cross was uppermost. There is reason to think that cloth flags of this design were employed during the 17th century for unofficial use on Scottish vessels at sea.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Smith_1973_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_1973-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> This flag\'s design is also described in the 1704 edition of <i>The Present State of the Universe</i> by <a href="/wiki/John_Beaumont_(geologist)" title="John Beaumont (geologist)">John Beaumont</a>, which contains as an appendix <i>The Ensigns, Colours or Flags of the Ships at Sea: Belonging to The several Princes and States in the World</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Engraving of a castle on top of a steep hill, above the title &quot;The North East View of Edinburgh Castle&quot;. On the castle flies a large Union Flag with Scottish saltire part of flag most visible." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg/220px-Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg/330px-Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg/440px-Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6753" data-file-height="4205" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Castle_John_Slezer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Slezer" title="John Slezer">Slezer\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Castle" title="Edinburgh Castle">Edinburgh Castle</a> c.1693 depicting the Scottish Union Flag.<sup id="cite_ref-slezer_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slezer-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div><p>On land, evidence confirming the use of this flag appears in the depiction of <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Castle" title="Edinburgh Castle">Edinburgh Castle</a> by <a href="/wiki/John_Slezer" title="John Slezer">John Slezer</a>, in his series of <a href="/wiki/Engraving" title="Engraving">engravings</a> entitled <i>Theatrum Scotiae</i>, c. 1693. Appearing in later editions of <i>Theatrum Scotiae</i>, the <i>North East View of Edinburgh Castle</i> engraving depicts the <i><a href="/wiki/Scotch_(adjective)" title="Scotch (adjective)">Scotch</a></i> (to use the appropriate adjective of that period) version of the Union Flag flying from the Palace block of the Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On the <i>North Prospect of the City of Edenburgh</i> engraving, the flag is indistinct.<sup id="cite_ref-north_prospect_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-north_prospect-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 April 1707, just two weeks prior to the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union</a> coming into effect, and with Sir Henry St George, <a href="/wiki/Garter_King_of_Arms" class="mw-redirect" title="Garter King of Arms">Garter King of Arms</a>, having presented several designs of flag to <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a> and her <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council">Privy Council</a> for consideration, the flag for the soon to be unified <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> was chosen. At the suggestion of the Scots representatives, the designs for consideration included that version of Union Jack showing the Cross of Saint Andrew uppermost; identified as being the "<i>Scotts union flagg as said to be used by the Scotts</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-de_Burton_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Burton-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> However, the Queen and her Council approved Sir Henry\'s original effort, numbered "one".<sup id="cite_ref-de_Burton_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Burton-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A manuscript compiled in 1785 by William Fox and in possession of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_Research_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag Research Center">Flag Research Center</a> includes a full plate showing "<i>the scoth </i>&#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93;<i> union</i>" flag. This could imply that there was still some use of a Scottish variant before the addition of the cross of St Patrick to the Union Flag in 1801.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_1973_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_1973-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_1801">Since 1801</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Since 1801">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_(HEGG_446).jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_%28HEGG_446%29.jpeg/170px-North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_%28HEGG_446%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_%28HEGG_446%29.jpeg/255px-North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_%28HEGG_446%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_%28HEGG_446%29.jpeg/340px-North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_%28HEGG_446%29.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="382" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:North-West_Mounted_Police_standing_next_to_American_and_British_flags_marking_the_boundary_between_Alaska_and_British_Columbia_(HEGG_446).jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1899 photograph of the British and American flags on the border between British Columbia and Alaska</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coloured_illustration_of_Anzac_troops_after_the_fighting_at_Gallipoli_during_World_War_I_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Coloured_illustration_of_Anzac_troops_after_the_fighting_at_Gallipoli_during_World_War_I_%281%29.jpg/170px-Coloured_illustration_of_Anzac_troops_after_the_fighting_at_Gallipoli_during_World_War_I_%281%29.jpg"
