1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Coloured_illustration_of_Anzac_troops_after_the_fighting_at_Gallipoli_during_World_War_I_%281%29.jpg/340px-Coloured_illustration_of_Anzac_troops_after_the_fighting_at_Gallipoli_during_World_War_I_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="373" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coloured_illustration_of_Anzac_troops_after_the_fighting_at_Gallipoli_during_World_War_I_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>-era depiction of the Union flag</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk,_June_3,_1920.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk%2C_June_3%2C_1920.png/170px-A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk%2C_June_3%2C_1920.png" width="170" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk%2C_June_3%2C_1920.png/255px-A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk%2C_June_3%2C_1920.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk%2C_June_3%2C_1920.png/340px-A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk%2C_June_3%2C_1920.png 2x" data-file-width="1853" data-file-height="1514" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_group_of_women_on_the_sidewalk,_June_3,_1920.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesters tearing up a Union flag in 1920</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:After_May_5th_1945_(10051164425).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/After_May_5th_1945_%2810051164425%29.jpg/220px-After_May_5th_1945_%2810051164425%29.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/After_May_5th_1945_%2810051164425%29.jpg/330px-After_May_5th_1945_%2810051164425%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/After_May_5th_1945_%2810051164425%29.jpg/440px-After_May_5th_1945_%2810051164425%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:After_May_5th_1945_(10051164425).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Large Union flag in Copenhagen after the <a href="/wiki/Denmark_in_World_War_II" title="Denmark in World War II">liberation of Denmark</a> (May 1945)</div></div></div>\n<p>The current and second Union Jack dates from 1 January 1801 with the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1800" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Union 1800">Act of Union 1800</a>, which merged the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a>. The new design added a red <a href="/wiki/Saltire" title="Saltire">saltire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Patrick&#39;s Flag">cross of Saint Patrick</a>, for Ireland. This is <a href="/wiki/Counterchanging" class="mw-redirect" title="Counterchanging">counterchanged</a> with the saltire of St Andrew, such that the white always follows the red clockwise. The arrangement has introduced a requirement to display the flag "the right way up"; see <a href="#Specifications_for_flag_use">specifications for flag use</a>, below. As with the red cross, so too the red saltire is separated by a white fimbriation from the blue field.<sup id="cite_ref-Flagsofworld_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flagsofworld-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This fimbriation is repeated for symmetry on the white portion of the saltire, which thereby appears wider than the red portion. The fimbriation of the cross of St George separates its red from the red of the saltire.\n</p><p>Apart from the Union Jack, Saint Patrick\'s cross has seldom been used to represent Ireland, and with little popular recognition or enthusiasm; it is usually considered to derive from the arms of the powerful <a href="/wiki/FitzGerald" class="mw-redirect" title="FitzGerald">FitzGerald</a> family rather than any association with the saint.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flag_speculation_after_Irish_independence">Flag speculation after Irish independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Flag speculation after Irish independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a> was concluded on 6 December 1921 and the creation of the new <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> was an imminent prospect, the question arose as to whether the cross of Saint Patrick should remain in the Union Jack. <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that on 22 January 1922:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>At the College of Arms it was stated that certain modifications were under consideration and that if any action were taken it would be done by the King in Council. No parliamentary action would be necessary. Heraldry experts say that alterations in arms are very expensive. Some years ago there was a demand from Irish quarters that the blue ground of the golden harp on the royal standard should be changed to green. It was then estimated that the alteration would cost at least \xc2\xa32,000,000. To remove all reference to Ireland from the present Union Jack and Royal Arms would be vastly more expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>There was some speculation on the matter in British dominions also, with one New Zealand paper reporting that:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>...the removal of the cross of St. Patrick Cross after 120 years will transform the appearance of the flag. It will certainly become a flag under which great victories were won in the seventeenth and eighteenth centuries, but to most minds the sentimental loss will be great. Probably it will be found that the deletion is not absolutely necessary. Other possible changes include the abolition of the title of the United Kingdom, and the removal of the harp from the Royal Standard and the Coat of Arms, and the substitution of the Ulster emblem.<sup id="cite_ref-ashburton_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ashburton-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>However, the fact that it was likely that <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> would choose not to remain part of the Irish Free State after its foundation and remain in the United Kingdom, gave better grounds for keeping the cross of St. Patrick in the Union Jack. In this regard, <a href="/wiki/Sir_James_Craig" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir James Craig">Sir James Craig</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Prime Minister of Northern Ireland">Prime Minister of Northern Ireland</a> remarked in December 1921 that he and his government were "glad to think that our decision [to remain part of United Kingdom] will obviate the necessity of mutilating the Union Jack."<sup id="cite_ref-ulster_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ulster-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Though remaining within the United Kingdom, the new government of Northern Ireland dispensed with the St Patrick\'s Saltire in favour of <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Flag of Northern Ireland">a new flag</a> derived from the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burke" title="House of Burke">coat-of-arm of the Burkes</a>, Earls of Ulster, and quite similar to England\'s St George\'s Cross.\n</p><p>Ultimately, when the British <a href="/wiki/Home_secretary" class="mw-redirect" title="Home secretary">home secretary</a> was asked on 7 December 1922 (the day after the Irish Free State was established) whether the <a href="/wiki/Garter_Principal_King_of_Arms" title="Garter Principal King of Arms">Garter King of Arms</a> was to issue any regulations with reference to the Union Jack, the response was no and the flag has never been changed.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Question_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Question Time">D\xc3\xa1il question</a> in 1961 mooted raising the removal of the cross of St Patrick with the British government; Frank Aiken, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Trade" title="Minister for Foreign Affairs and Trade">Irish minister for external affairs</a>, declined to "waste time on heraldic disputations".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaigns_for_a_new_Union_Flag">Campaigns for a new Union Flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Campaigns for a new Union Flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Union_Flag_(including_Wales).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Union_Flag_%28including_Wales%29.svg/220px-Union_Flag_%28including_Wales%29.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Union_Flag_%28including_Wales%29.svg/330px-Union_Flag_%28including_Wales%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Union_Flag_%28including_Wales%29.svg/440px-Union_Flag_%28including_Wales%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Union_Flag_(including_Wales).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Union Flag with the red dragon from the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Wales" title="Flag of Wales">flag of Wales</a> added in the centre.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2003, a private individual started a campaign&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 dubbed "reflag" or "Union Black"&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 to interpret the Union Flag in a racial context, and introduce black stripes in it. The proposal was universally met with opposition and was denounced by <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">MSP</a> <a href="/wiki/Phil_Gallie" title="Phil Gallie">Phil Gallie</a> as "ridiculous tokenism [that] would do nothing to stamp out racism".<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The campaign is now defunct.\n</p><p>Since there is no uniquely Welsh element in the Union Jack, <a href="/wiki/Wrexham" title="Wrexham">Wrexham</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a> <a href="/wiki/Ian_Lucas" title="Ian Lucas">Ian Lucas</a> proposed on 27 November 2007 in a <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> debate that the Union Flag be combined with the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Wales" title="Flag of Wales">Welsh flag</a> to reflect Wales\' status within the UK, and that the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Dragon" title="Welsh Dragon">red dragon</a> be added to the Union Flag\'s red, white, and blue pattern.<sup id="cite_ref-welsh_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-welsh-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He said the Union Jack currently only represented the other three UK nations, and <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Culture,_Media_and_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Department for Culture, Media and Sport">Minister for Culture, Creative Industries and Tourism</a> <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Hodge" title="Margaret Hodge">Margaret Hodge</a> conceded that Lucas had raised a valid point for debate. She said, "the Government is keen to make the Union Flag a positive symbol of Britishness reflecting the diversity of our country today and encouraging people to take pride in our flag." This development sparked design contests with entries from all over the world; some of the entries incorporated red dragons and even <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> characters and <a href="/wiki/Leek#Cultural_significance" title="Leek">leeks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-face_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-face-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-japan_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-japan-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The lack of any Welsh symbol or colours in the flag is due to Wales already being part of the Kingdom of England when the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Great_Britain" title="Flag of Great Britain">flag of Great Britain</a> was created in 1606.\n</p><p>In the run-up to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">2014 Scottish independence referendum</a>, various non-official suggestions were made for how the flag could be redesigned without the St Andrew\'s Cross in the event that Scotland left the Union. However, as Scotland voted against independence the issue did not arise.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brexit">Brexit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Brexit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">UK referendum</a> on membership of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> which resulted in a vote to <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">leave</a>, the Union Flag became a symbol of <a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">euroscepticism</a> in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> in August 2016 as hundreds of local businesses along the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Riviera" title="Italian Riviera">Italian riviera</a> hoisted the flags as a protest against the implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Services_in_the_Internal_Market_Directive_2006" title="Services in the Internal Market Directive 2006">Services in the Internal Market Directive 2006</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ghiglione_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ghiglione-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2016, anti-Brexit campaigners planned to fly 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">European Union flags</a> on the last night of the <a href="/wiki/The_Proms" title="The Proms">BBC Proms</a>, in response, <a href="/wiki/Leave.EU" title="Leave.EU">Leave.EU</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/Arron_Banks" title="Arron Banks">Arron Banks</a> announced he planned to fund and give away 10,000 Union Flags to concert-goers.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portadown_(26),_September_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Portadown_%2826%29%2C_September_2009.JPG/220px-Portadown_%2826%29%2C_September_2009.JPG" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Portadown_%2826%29%2C_September_2009.JPG/330px-Portadown_%2826%29%2C_September_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Portadown_%2826%29%2C_September_2009.JPG/440px-Portadown_%2826%29%2C_September_2009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portadown_(26),_September_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Union Flag on display in <a href="/wiki/Portadown" title="Portadown">Portadown</a> in Northern Ireland. Northern Ireland has been part of the United Kingdom in its current form since 1921.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Union Jack is used as a <a href="/wiki/Jack_(flag)" title="Jack (flag)">jack</a> by commissioned warships and submarines of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, and by commissioned <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> vessels. When at anchor or alongside, it is flown from the <a href="/wiki/Jackstaff" title="Jackstaff">jackstaff</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Bow_(ship)" title="Bow (ship)">bow</a> of the ship. When a ship is underway, the Union Jack is only flown from the jackstaff when the ship is dressed for a special occasion, such as the Queen\'s official birthday.\n</p><p>The Union Jack is worn at the masthead of a ship to indicate the presence of the Sovereign or an <a href="/wiki/Admiral_of_the_Fleet_(Royal_Navy)" title="Admiral of the Fleet (Royal Navy)">Admiral of the Fleet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTWsea_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTWsea-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The Union Flag may also be flown from the yardarm to indicate that a <a href="/wiki/Court-martial" title="Court-martial">court-martial</a> is in progress, though these are now normally held at shore establishments.\n</p><p>No law has been passed making the Union Jack the national flag of the United Kingdom: it has become one through precedent. Its first recorded recognition as a national flag came in 1908, when it was stated in Parliament that "the Union Jack should be regarded as the National flag".<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> A more categorical statement was made by <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Home_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for the Home Department">Home Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Gilmour,_2nd_Baronet" title="Sir John Gilmour, 2nd Baronet">Sir John Gilmour</a>, in 1933 when he stated that "the Union Flag is the national flag and may properly be flown by any British subject on land."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Civilian use is permitted on land, but use of the unmodified flag at sea is restricted to military vessels. Unauthorised use of the flag in the 17th century to avoid paying harbour duties&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 a privilege restricted to naval ships&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 caused James\'s successor, <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a>, to order that use of the flag on naval vessels be restricted to His Majesty\'s ships "upon pain of Our high displeasure."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It remains a criminal offence under the Merchant Shipping Act 1995<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> to display the Union Flag (other than the "pilot jack"&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 see below) from a British ship. Naval ships will fly the <a href="/wiki/White_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="White ensign">white ensign</a>, merchant and private boats can fly the <a href="/wiki/Red_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="Red ensign">red ensign</a>, others with special permission such as naval yacht clubs can fly the <a href="/wiki/Blue_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue ensign">blue ensign</a>. All of the coloured ensigns contain the union flag as part of the design.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Court_of_the_Lord_Lyon" title="Court of the Lord Lyon">Court of the Lord Lyon</a>, which has legal jurisdiction in heraldic matters in Scotland, confirms that the Union Jack "is the correct flag for all citizens and corporate bodies of the United Kingdom to fly to demonstrate their loyalty and their nationality."<sup id="cite_ref-lordlyon_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lordlyon-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Australia" title="Flag of Australia">current national flag</a> gradually replaced the Union Flag. When it formally created the national flag in the <a href="/wiki/Flags_Act_1953" title="Flags Act 1953">Flags Act 1953</a>, section 8 of that Act specified that "this Act does not affect the right or privilege of a person to fly the Union Jack." The Union Jack continued to be used for a period thereafter as a national flag.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_New_Zealand" title="Flag of New Zealand">current national flag</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> was given official standing under the New Zealand Ensign Act in 1902, but similarly to Australia the Union Jack continued to be used in some contexts as a national flag.<sup id="cite_ref-nzflag_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nzflag-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 February 2008, <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Rosindell" title="Andrew Rosindell">Andrew Rosindell</a> introduced the \'Union Flag Bill\' as a <a href="/wiki/Private_member%27s_bill" title="Private member&#39;s bill">private member\'s bill</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Ten_Minute_Rule" title="Ten Minute Rule">10 Minute Rule</a> in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>. The Bill sought to formalise the position of the Union Flag as the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Flag of the United Kingdom">national flag of the UK</a> in law, to remove legal obstacles to its regular display and to officially recognise the name \'Union Jack\' as having equal status with \'Union Flag\'. However the Bill did not receive its <a href="/wiki/Second_reading" class="mw-redirect" title="Second reading">second reading</a> by the end of that <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_session" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary session">parliamentary session</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bill_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Union Jack was introduced into <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> in 1795, and except for the period 1803-06, it was an official flag until 1957.  \n</p><p>When the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> was established in 1910, the Union Jack was treated as its official flag. \n</p><p>The continued use of the Union Jack as national flag became an issue in the 1920s, when the government proposed to introduce a National Flag of the Union.  A compromise was reached in which both flags were flown on official buildings.  The Union Nationality and Flags Act 1927 provided that the flags of the Union were (a) the Union Jack, to denote the association with the other members of the British Commonwealth of Nations, and (b) the new <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_South_Africa_(1928-1994)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag of South Africa (1928-1994)"> National Flag</a>.  The Union Jack was to be flown alongside the National Flag at the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa" title="Parliament of South Africa"> Houses of Parliament</a>, from the principal government buildings in the capitals, at Union ports, on government offices abroad, and at such other places as the government might determine.<sup id="cite_ref-unfa_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unfa-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-sava_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sava-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>  This dual arrangement was effective from 31 May 1928.\n</p><p>Instructions issued in 1931 confirmed the places where both flags were to be flown.  In addition to those already mentioned, they were the <a href="/wiki/Union_Buildings" title="Union Buildings">Union Buildings</a> (Pretoria), the head offices of the four provincial administrations, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Supreme Court of South Africa"> supreme courts</a>, certain <a href="/wiki/Magistrate%27s_court_(South_Africa)" title="Magistrate&#39;s court (South Africa)"> magistrates\' courts</a>, customs houses, and three buildings in <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> (the general post office, the <a href="/wiki/Durban_railway_station" title="Durban railway station"> railway station</a>, and the local <a href="/wiki/Natal_Command" title="Natal Command"> military district headquarters</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-iff31_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iff31-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-sava_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sava-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under these arrangements, the Union Jack was subordinate to the National Flag.  As the two flags had to be the same size, it meant that the Union Jack was made in the ratio 2:3 rather than the usual 1:2.<sup id="cite_ref-iff_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iff-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sava_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sava-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The flying of the Union Jack alongside the National Flag ended on 6 April 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-faa_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faa-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>   \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York,_Toronto.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York%2C_Toronto.JPG/220px-Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York%2C_Toronto.JPG" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York%2C_Toronto.JPG/330px-Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York%2C_Toronto.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York%2C_Toronto.JPG/440px-Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York%2C_Toronto.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1524" data-file-height="1065" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pre-1801_Union_Flag_at_Fort_York,_Toronto.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pre-1801 Union Flag flies at <a href="/wiki/Fort_York" title="Fort York">Fort York</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> base in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The predecessor of the Union Jack, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Great_Britain" title="Flag of Great Britain">flag of Great Britain</a>, came into use in what is now Canada at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Scottish</a> settlement of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> in 1621.<sup id="cite_ref-pch_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pch-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The Union Flag was also the official flag of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</a> and continued in use there after <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland</a> became a Canadian province. The province adopted <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Flag of Newfoundland and Labrador">its own flag</a> in 1980, employing a design based on that of the Union Flag.\n</p><p>At the close of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Canadian_Flag_Debate" title="Great Canadian Flag Debate">Great Canadian Flag Debate</a> in 1964, which resulted in the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Canada" title="Flag of Canada">Maple Leaf Flag</a> as Canada\'s national flag the following year, a resolution was passed by both houses of the Canadian parliament naming the Union Flag as the <i>Royal Union Flag</i> and designating it as the symbol of Canada\'s membership of the Commonwealth and its allegiance to <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm#The_Crown_in_the_Commonwealth_realms" title="Commonwealth realm">the Crown</a>. The move was a concession given to conservatives, who preferred to keep the old flag, with its Union Flag in the canton. A federal directive says the Royal Union Flag is to be flown alongside the Maple Leaf Flag at federal government buildings, federally-operated airports and military bases, and at the masthead of <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Navy">Her Majesty\'s Canadian ships</a> within Canadian waters<sup id="cite_ref-DCH_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCH-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> on three days of the year: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Day" title="Commonwealth Day">Commonwealth Day</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">Canadian monarch\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Official_Birthday#Canada" title="Queen&#39;s Official Birthday">official birthday</a>, and the anniversary of the enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DCH_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCH-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The flag is to be raised only where there is more than one flag pole, to ensure the flag of Canada is not removed. The directive is sometimes followed, sometimes not.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ratios">Other ratios</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other ratios">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table style="width:218px; float:right; clear:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em; background:#f9f9f9; border:1px #aaaaaa solid; border-collapse:collapse; font-size:90%; line-height:16px;"><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:center;padding:3px;"><table style="margin: auto; background:#f9f9f9; border: 1px #aaaaaa solid; border-collapse: collapse;"><tbody><tr><td style="padding:0px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom_(3-5).svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of the United Kingdom (3-5).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom_%283-5%29.svg/175px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom_%283-5%29.svg.png" width="175" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom_%283-5%29.svg/264px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom_%283-5%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom_%283-5%29.svg/350px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom_%283-5%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></td></tr></tbody></table><a href="/wiki/War_flag" title="War flag">War flag</a> variant <a href="/wiki/File:FIAV_001000.svg" class="image"><img alt="FIAV 001000.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/FIAV_001000.svg/23px-FIAV_001000.svg.png" width="23" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/FIAV_001000.svg/35px-FIAV_001000.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/FIAV_001000.svg/46px-FIAV_001000.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="210" /></a><br /> Proportions: 3:5</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Although the most common ratio is 1:2, other ratios exist. The Royal Navy\'s flag code book, BR20 <i>Flags of All Nations</i>, states that both 1:2 and 3:5 versions are official.<sup id="cite_ref-35variant_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35variant-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The 3:5 version is most commonly used by the British Army and is sometimes known as the <a href="/wiki/War_flag" title="War flag">War flag</a>. In this version the innermost points of the lower left and upper right diagonals of the St Patrick\'s cross are cut off or truncated.\n</p><p>The Queen\'s Harbour Master\'s flag, like the Pilot Jack, is a 1:2 flag that contains a white-bordered Union Flag that is longer than 1:2. The jacks of ships flying variants of the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ensign" title="Blue Ensign">Blue Ensign</a> are square and have a square Union Flag in the canton.<sup id="cite_ref-35variant_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35variant-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Regimental_colours#British_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Regimental colours">Queen\'s Colours of Army regiments</a> are 36 by 43 inches (910&#160;mm \xc3\x97&#160;1,090&#160;mm); on them, the bars of the cross and saltire are of equal width; so are their respective fimbriations, which are very narrow.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As stated above, the Union Jacks flown alongside the National Flag in South Africa between 1928 and 1957 were 2:3 flags.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_in_other_flags">Use in other flags</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Use in other flags">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_with_the_Union_Jack_displayed_on_their_flag" title="List of countries and territories with the Union Jack displayed on their flag">List of countries and territories with the Union Jack displayed on their flag</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_nations_and_regions">Other nations and regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Other nations and regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit">improve Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(May 2011)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Australia_(converted).svg" class="image"><img alt="Dark blue flag with six white stars and Union Flag as top-left quarter" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Australia_(converted).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Australia" title="Flag of Australia">flag of Australia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Union Flag was found in the <i><a href="/wiki/Flag_terminology" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag terminology">canton</a></i> (upper left-hand quarter) of the flags of many colonies of Britain, while the <i><a href="/wiki/Field_(heraldry)" title="Field (heraldry)">field</a></i> (background) of their flags was the colour of the <a href="/wiki/British_ensigns#History" class="mw-redirect" title="British ensigns">naval ensign</a> flown by the particular <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> squadron that patrolled that region of the world. Nations and colonies that have used the Union Flag at some stage have included <a href="/wiki/Aden" title="Aden">Aden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceylon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceylon">Ceylon</a> (now Sri Lanka), <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_East_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="British East Africa">British East Africa (Kenya Colony)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(British_colony)" title="Gold Coast (British colony)">Gold Coast (Ghana)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lagos" title="Lagos">Lagos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penang" title="Penang">Penang (Malaysia)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somaliland" title="Somaliland">Somaliland</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanganyika" title="Tanganyika">Tanganyika</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weihaiwei_under_British_rule" title="Weihaiwei under British rule">Weihaiwei</a>. As former British Empire nations were granted independence, these and other versions of the Union Flag were decommissioned. The most recent decommissioning of the Union Flag came on 1 July 1997, when the former <a href="/wiki/History_of_Colonial_Hong_Kong_(1800s%E2%80%931930s)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Colonial Hong Kong (1800s\xe2\x80\x931930s)">Dependent Territory of Hong Kong</a> was handed over to the People\'s Republic of China.\n</p><p>All administrative regions and territories of the United Kingdom fly the Union Jack in some form, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Gibraltar" title="Flag of Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> (other than the government ensign) and the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Dependencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Dependencies">Crown Dependencies</a>. Outside the UK, the Union Jack is usually part of a special <a href="/wiki/Ensign" title="Ensign">ensign</a> in which it is placed in the upper left hand corner of a blue field, with a signifying crest in the bottom right.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/220px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/330px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg/440px-Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1815" data-file-height="1432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Mees_Flags_of_A_Free_Empire_1910_Cornell_CUL_PJM_1167_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> (as of 1910)</div></div></div>\n<p>Four former British colonies in Oceania which are now independent countries incorporate the Union Jack as part of their national flags: Australia, New Zealand and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, which have retained the monarchy; and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, which <a href="/wiki/1987_Fijian_coups_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1987 Fijian coups d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat">abolished the monarchy in 1987</a>.\n</p><p>In former British colonies, the Union Jack was used semi-interchangeably with territorial flags for significant parts of their early history. This was the case in Canada until the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Canada" title="Flag of Canada">Maple Leaf Flag</a> in 1965, but it is still used in the flags of a number of Canadian provinces such as <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>. <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a> uses a modified version of the Union Flag, once the flag of the province.\n</p><p>Along with the national flag, many other <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_flags" title="List of Australian flags">Australian</a> flags retain the use of the Union Jack, including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy_Ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Australian Navy Ensign">Royal Australian Navy Ensign</a> (also known as the Australian White Ensign), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Air_Force_Ensign" title="Royal Australian Air Force Ensign">Royal Australian Air Force Ensign</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Red_Ensign" title="Australian Red Ensign">Australian Red Ensign</a> (for use by merchant and private vessels), and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Civil_Aviation_Ensign" title="Australian Civil Aviation Ensign">Australian Civil Aviation Ensign</a>. The flags of all six Australian States retain the Union Jack in the canton, as do some regional flags such as the Upper and Lower <a href="/wiki/Murray_River_Flag" title="Murray River Flag">Murray River Flags</a>. The Vice-Regal flags of the State Governors also use the Union Jack.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(historical_territory)" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque Country (historical territory)">Basque Country\'s</a> flag, the <a href="/wiki/Ikurri%C3%B1a" title="Ikurri\xc3\xb1a">Ikurri\xc3\xb1a</a>, is also loosely based on the Union Jack, reflecting the significant commercial ties between <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> and Britain at the time the <a href="/wiki/Ikurri%C3%B1a" title="Ikurri\xc3\xb1a">Ikurri\xc3\xb1a</a> was designed in 1894. The <a href="/wiki/Miskito_people" title="Miskito people">Miskito</a> people sometimes use a similar flag that also incorporates the Union Jack in its canton, due to long periods of contact in the <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">Mosquito Coast</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Hawaii.svg" class="image"><img alt="Thin red white and blue horizontal stripes with Union Flag as top-left quarter." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Flag_of_Hawaii.svg/220px-Flag_of_Hawaii.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Flag_of_Hawaii.svg/330px-Flag_of_Hawaii.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Flag_of_Hawaii.svg/440px-Flag_of_Hawaii.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Hawaii.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Ka Hae Hawai<span class="unicode">&#x2bb;</span>i</i>, or the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Hawaii" title="Flag of Hawaii">flag of Hawaii</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Union Jack was used by the United States in its first flag, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Union_Flag" title="Grand Union Flag">Grand Union Flag</a>. This flag was of a similar design to the one used by the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a>. Hawaii, a state of the United States but located in the central Pacific, incorporates the Union Jack in its <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Hawaii" title="Flag of Hawaii">state flag</a>. According to one story, the King of Hawaii asked the British mariner, <a href="/wiki/George_Vancouver" title="George Vancouver">George Vancouver</a>, during a stop in Lahaina, what the piece of cloth flying from his ship was. Vancouver replied that it represented his king\'s authority. The Hawaiian king then adopted and flew the flag as a symbol of his own royal authority not recognising its national derivation. Hawaii\'s flag represents the only current use of the Union Jack in any American state flag.\n</p><p>Also in the United States, the Union Flag of 1606 is incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Baton_Rouge,_Louisiana" title="Flag of Baton Rouge, Louisiana">flag of Baton Rouge</a>, the capital city of Louisiana. Baton Rouge was a British colony from the time of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War">Seven Years\' War</a> until the end of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, when it was captured by Spanish and American forces. Symbols from the colonial powers France and Spain are also incorporated into the Baton Rouge flag. <a href="/wiki/Taunton,_Massachusetts" title="Taunton, Massachusetts">Taunton, Massachusetts</a>, USA, has in recent years<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2013)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> used <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Taunton,_Massachusetts" title="Flag of Taunton, Massachusetts">a flag with the old style Union Flag</a>.  Likewise, <a href="/wiki/Westmoreland_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Westmoreland County, Pennsylvania">Westmoreland County, Pennsylvania</a>, has been known to fly a flag containing the King\'s Colours since 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Union Jack also appeared on both the 1910\xe2\x80\x931928 and 1928\xe2\x80\x931994 <a href="/wiki/South_African_Flag#History" class="mw-redirect" title="South African Flag">flags</a> of South Africa. The <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_Red_Ensign" title="South Africa Red Ensign">1910\xe2\x80\x931928 flag</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Red_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="Red ensign">red ensign</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union</a> coat of arms in the fly. The 1928\xe2\x80\x931994 flag, based on the <a href="/wiki/Prinsenvlag#The_Prince&#39;s_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Prinsenvlag">Prinsenvlag</a> and commonly known as the <i>oranje-blanje-blou</i> (orange-white-blue), contained the Union Jack as part of a central motif at par with the flags of the two <a href="/wiki/Boer" title="Boer">Boer</a> republics of the <a href="/wiki/Orange_Free_State" title="Orange Free State">Orange Free State</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">Transvaal</a>. To keep any one of the three flags from having precedence, the Union Jack is spread horizontally from the Orange Free State flag towards the hoist; closest to the hoist, it is in the superior position but since it is reversed it does not precede the other flags.\n</p><p>The coat of arms of the <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chilean</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Coquimbo" title="Coquimbo">Coquimbo</a> features the Union Jack, owing to its historical commercial links to Britain.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303619">@media all and //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_South_Africa_%281928%E2%80%931994%29.svg/240px-Flag_of_South_Africa_%281928%E2%80%931994%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="396" /></a></div></div></div></div><div style="display:table-row;vertical-align:top"><div style="display:block;font-size:94%;padding:0px"><div class="gallerytext" style="min-height:1.6em;width:127px;line-height:1.3em;padding:2px 6px 1px 6px;margin:0px;border:none;border-width:0px"><i>Oranje-blanje-blou</i>, or the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_South_Africa_(1928%E2%80%931994)" title="Flag of South Africa (1928\xe2\x80\x931994)">Flag of South Africa (1928\xe2\x80\x931994)</a>&#160;</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ensigns">Ensigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ensigns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_ensigns" class="mw-redirect" title="British ensigns">British ensigns</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(May 2011)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Union Flag can be found in the canton of several of the <a href="/wiki/Ensign" title="Ensign">ensigns</a> flown by vessels and aircraft of the United Kingdom and its overseas territories. These are used in cases where it is illegal to fly the Union Flag, such as at sea from a ship other than a British warship. Normal practice for British ships is to fly the <a href="/wiki/White_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="White ensign">White ensign</a> (Royal Navy), the <a href="/wiki/Red_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="Red ensign">Red ensign</a> (Merchant and private boats) or the <a href="/wiki/Blue_ensign" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue ensign">Blue ensign</a> (government departments and public corporations). Similar ensigns are used by other countries (such as <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_Zealand_flags#Ensigns" title="List of New Zealand flags">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_flags#Military_and_naval_flags" title="List of Australian flags">Australia</a>) with the Union Flag in the canton. Other Commonwealth countries (such as <a href="/wiki/Indian_Military_Flags" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Military Flags">India</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Jamaican_flags#Ensigns" title="List of Jamaican flags">Jamaica</a>) may follow similar ensign etiquette as the UK, replacing the Union Flag with their own national flag.\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303619"/><div class="mw-module-gallery" style="display:table;background:transparent;margin-top:0.5em"><div style="display:table-row"><div
