6px;margin:0px;border:none;border-width:0px">Fiji Civil Ensign.&#160;</div></div></div></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pilot_or_Civil_Jack">Pilot or Civil Jack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Pilot or Civil Jack">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Union Flag with thick white border comprising about half of the area of the flag." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/220px-Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/330px-Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/440px-Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Civil_Jack_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Union Jack with a white border.</div></div></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(May 2011)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The flag in a white border occasionally seen on merchant ships was sometimes referred to as the <b>Pilot Jack</b>. It can be traced back to 1823 when it was created as a signal flag, never intended as a civil jack. A book<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="What book? (September 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> issued to British <a href="/wiki/Consul" title="Consul">consuls</a> in 1855 states that the white bordered Union Flag is to be hoisted for a pilot. Although there was some ambiguity regarding the legality of it being flown for any other purpose on civilian vessels, its use as an ensign or jack was established well in advance of the 1864 Act that designated the <a href="/wiki/Red_Ensign" title="Red Ensign">Red Ensign</a> for merchant shipping. In 1970, the white-bordered Union Flag ceased to be the signal for a pilot, but references to it as national colours were not removed from the current Merchant Shipping Act and it was legally interpreted as a flag that could be flown on a merchant ship, as a jack if desired. This status was confirmed to an extent by the Merchant Shipping (Registration, etc.) Act 1993 and the consolidating Merchant Shipping Act 1995 which, in Section 4, Subsection 1, prohibits the use of any distinctive national colours or those used or resembling flags or pendants on Her Majesty\'s Ships, "except the <a href="/wiki/Red_Ensign" title="Red Ensign">Red Ensign</a>, the Union flag (commonly known as the Union Jack) with a white border", and some other exceptions permitted elsewhere in the Acts. However, Section 2 regards the "British flag", and states that "The flag which every British ship is entitled to fly is the Red Ensign (without any defacement or modification) and, subject to (a warrant from Her Majesty or from the Secretary of State, or an Order of Council from her Majesty regarding a defaced <a href="/wiki/Red_Ensign" title="Red Ensign">Red Ensign</a>), no other colours."<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Many civil vessels continue to fly the white bordered Union Flag without official opposition, making it the <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> Civil Jack.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg/220px-Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg/330px-Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg/440px-Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hudson%27s_Bay_Company_Flag.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Flag of the Hudson&#39;s Bay Company">Flag of the Hudson\'s Bay Company</a> which originated from its days as a British trading company.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson&#39;s Bay Company">Hudson\'s Bay Company</a> (HBC) was one of a few non-government institutions using the Union Jack in part of the flag. HBC rival <a href="/wiki/North_West_Company" title="North West Company">North West Company</a> had a similar flag as well. The HBC jack is no longer in use and replaced with a corporate flag featuring the company\'s coat of arms.\n</p><p>The Union Jack is the third <a href="/wiki/Quartering_(heraldry)" title="Quartering (heraldry)">quarter</a> of the 1939 <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Alabama" title="Coat of arms of Alabama">coat of arms of Alabama</a>, representing British sovereignty over the state prior to 1783. The version used is the modern flag, whereas the 1707 flag would have been used in colonial Alabama.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flag_days">Flag days</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Flag days">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(February 2010)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In July 2007, the British prime minister at the time, <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a>, unveiled plans to have the Union Flag flown more often from government buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> While consultation on new guidelines is under way, the decision to fly the flag may be made by each government department.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Dated" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Dated"><span title="This assertion may no longer be correct \xe2\x80\x94 please check and update as needed. (September 2012)">old info</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Previously the flag was generally only flown on public buildings on days marking the birthdays of members of the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="British Royal Family">Royal Family</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wedding_anniversary" title="Wedding anniversary">wedding anniversary</a> of the monarch, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Day" title="Commonwealth Day">Commonwealth Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession Day">Accession Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coronation_Day" title="Coronation Day">Coronation Day</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Birthday" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Birthday">Queen\'s Official Birthday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Remembrance_Sunday" title="Remembrance Sunday">Remembrance Sunday</a>, and on the days of the State Opening and <a href="/wiki/Legislative_session#Common_procedure" title="Legislative session">prorogation</a> of Parliament. The Union Flag is flown at <a href="/wiki/Half_mast" class="mw-redirect" title="Half mast">half mast</a> from the announcement of the death of the Sovereign (save for Proclamation Day), or upon command of the Sovereign.<sup id="cite_ref-dcms_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dcms-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The current flag days where the Union Flag should be flown from government buildings throughout the UK are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>9 January (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Catherine,_Duchess_of_Cambridge" title="Catherine, Duchess of Cambridge">The Duchess of Cambridge</a>)</li>\n<li>20 January (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Sophie,_Countess_of_Wessex" title="Sophie, Countess of Wessex">The Countess of Wessex</a>)</li>\n<li>6 February (Anniversary of the accession of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">The Queen</a>)</li>\n<li>19 February (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">The Duke of York</a>)</li>\n<li>Second Monday in March (<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Day" title="Commonwealth Day">Commonwealth Day</a>)</li>\n<li>10 March (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Earl_of_Wessex" title="Prince Edward, Earl of Wessex">The Earl of Wessex</a>)</li>\n<li>21 April (The Queen\'s Birthday)</li>\n<li>9 May (<a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">Europe Day</a>)</li>\n<li>2 June (Anniversary of The Queen\'s coronation)</li>\n<li>10 June (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">The Duke of Edinburgh</a>)</li>\n<li>June (second Saturday)&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Birthday" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Birthday">The Queen\'s Official Birthday</a></li>\n<li>21 June (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">The Duke of Cambridge</a>)</li>\n<li>17 July (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Camilla,_Duchess_of_Cornwall" title="Camilla, Duchess of Cornwall">The Duchess of Cornwall</a>)</li>\n<li>15 August (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">The Princess Royal</a>)</li>\n<li>Second Sunday in November (<a href="/wiki/Remembrance_Sunday" title="Remembrance Sunday">Remembrance Sunday</a>)</li>\n<li>14 November (Birthday of <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">The Prince of Wales</a>)</li>\n<li>20 November (Anniversary of the wedding of The Queen and The Duke of Edinburgh)</li></ul>\n<p>In addition, the Union Flag should be flown in the following areas on specified days:\n</p>\n<ul><li>1 March (Wales only, for <a href="/wiki/Saint_David%27s_Day" title="Saint David&#39;s Day">St David\'s Day</a>)</li>\n<li>17 March (<a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> only, for <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="St Patrick&#39;s Day">St Patrick\'s Day</a>)</li>\n<li>23 April (England only, for <a href="/wiki/Saint_George%27s_Day" title="Saint George&#39;s Day">St George\'s Day</a>)</li>\n<li>The Day of the Opening of a Session of the Houses of Parliament, <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a> only</li>\n<li>The day of the prorogation of a Session of the Houses of Parliament, <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">Greater London</a> only .<sup id="cite_ref-dcms1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dcms1-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>On 30 November, (<a href="/wiki/Saint_Andrew%27s_Day" title="Saint Andrew&#39;s Day">St Andrew\'s Day</a>), the Union Flag can be flown in Scotland only where a building has more than one flagpole\xe2\x80\x94on this day the Saltire will not be lowered to make way for the Union Flag if there is only one flagpole.<sup id="cite_ref-scotland_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scotland-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> This difference arose after <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">Members of the Scottish Parliament</a> complained that Scotland was the only country in the world that could not fly its national flag on its national day. However, on 23 April, St George\'s Day, it is the Union Flag of the United Kingdom that is flown over United Kingdom\'s government offices in England.<sup id="cite_ref-agree_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agree-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Non-government organisations may fly the Union Flag whenever they choose.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_and_disposal">Usage and disposal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Usage and disposal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Union Flag has no official status in the United Kingdom, and there are no national regulations concerning its use or prohibitions against <a href="/wiki/Flag_desecration" title="Flag desecration">flag desecration</a>. In Northern Ireland, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Flags_Regulations_(Northern_Ireland)_2000&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Flags Regulations (Northern Ireland) 2000 (page does not exist)">Flags Regulations (Northern Ireland) 2000</a> provide for the flying of the flag on government buildings on certain occasions, when it is flown half mast, and how it is displayed with other flags.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Flags and Heraldry Committee, an <a href="/wiki/All-party_parliamentary_group" title="All-party parliamentary group">all-party parliamentary group</a> lobbying for official standards, cooperated with the <a href="/wiki/Flag_Institute" title="Flag Institute">Flag Institute</a> in 2010 to publish a set of recommended guidelines for the flag\'s display and use as a symbol.<sup id="cite_ref-FFitUK_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFitUK-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is no specific way in which the Union Flag should be folded <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States#Folding_for_storage" title="Flag of the United States">as there is with the United States Flag</a>. It is usually folded rectilinearly, with the hoist on the outside, to be easily reattached to the pole.<sup id="cite_ref-FFitUK_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFitUK-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fotw-canada_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fotw-canada-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Royal Navy Stores Duties Instructions, article 447, dated 26 February 1914, specified that flags condemned from further service use were to be torn up into small pieces and disposed of as rags (ADM 1/8369/56), not to be used for decoration or sold. The exception was flags that had flown in action: these could be framed and kept on board, or transferred to a "suitable place", such as a museum (ADM 1/8567/245).<sup id="cite_ref-Flagsofworld_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flagsofworld-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_names">Other names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>In Hong Kong and mainland China, the flag has the nickname <i>Rice-Character Flag</i> (\xe7\xb1\xb3\xe5\xad\x97\xe6\x97\x97; <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a> <a href="/wiki/Jyutping" title="Jyutping">Jyutping</a>: <i>mai5zi6kei4</i>, <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a> <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a>: <i>m\xc7\x90z\xc3\xacq\xc3\xad</i>) in Chinese, since the pattern looks like the Chinese character for "rice" (\xe7\xb1\xb3).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <i>Butcher\'s Apron</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejorative</a> term for the flag, common among <a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">Irish republicans</a>, citing the blood-streaked appearance of the flag and referring to atrocities committed in Ireland and other countries under British colonial rule.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Sandra_White" title="Sandra White">Sandra White</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">Member of the Scottish Parliament</a>, caused a furore when the term was used in a press release under her name. It was later blamed on the actions of a researcher, who resigned yet claimed that the comment had been approved by White.<sup id="cite_ref-apron_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apron-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Search_for_the_.22Eureka_Jack.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Search_for_the_&quot;Eureka_Jack&quot;">Search for the "Eureka Jack"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Search for the &quot;Eureka Jack&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Black and white drawing of two flags flying on a flagpole: above a white cross on a dark background with five star outlines over the cross; below the Union Jack." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg/250px-EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg" width="250" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg/375px-EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg/500px-EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="454" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EUREKA_JACK_INSET.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>There is a possibility based on the first reports of the battle that a second, Union Flag, was being flown on 3 December 1854 by the rebels besieged at the Eureka Stockade.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2013 the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Flag_Society" title="Australian Flag Society">Australian Flag Society</a> announced a worldwide quest and a <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">A$</a>10,000 reward for information leading to the discovery of the Union Jack which was reportedly hoisted beneath the <a href="/wiki/Eureka_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Eureka flag">Eureka flag</a> at the Battle of the <a href="/wiki/Eureka_Stockade" class="mw-redirect" title="Eureka Stockade">Eureka Stockade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cowie_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cowie-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As the de facto national flag of the United Kingdom, the Union Jack serves as a patriotic or nationalist symbol, and can also carry associations of militarism and imperialism.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winston Churchill wrote about the use of the Union Jack as a symbol connected to <a href="/wiki/British_nationalism" title="British nationalism">British nationalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a>. In March 1899 the young Churchill wrote to his mother from India about her plans to produce a new trans-Atlantic magazine, to be called <i>The Anglo-Saxon Review</i>. The drawing at the end of this letter was deliberately mischievous, teasing her for going down-market, and in the accompanying letter he wrote, \'Your title "The Anglo Saxon" with its motto "Blood is thicker than water" only needs the Union Jack &amp; the Star Spangled Banner crossed on the cover to be suited to one of Harmsworth\'s [a leading British newspaper owner] cheap Imperialist productions.\'<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Union Flag has been a prominent symbol in the sphere of <a href="/wiki/Fashion" title="Fashion">fashion</a> since the <a href="/wiki/British_Invasion" title="British Invasion">British Invasion</a> movement of the 1960s, in a similar manner to the American <a href="/wiki/Stars_and_Stripes_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Stars and Stripes flag">Stars and Stripes flag</a>. A notable increase in popularity was seen in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> following the 2012 summer Olympics, with clothing, nail decoration, tattoos, and hairstyles in youths being observed featuring the pattern.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Commonly the Union Flag is used on computer software and Internet pages as an <a href="/wiki/Computer_icon" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer icon">icon</a> representing a choice of the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> where a choice among multiple languages may be presented to the user. The flag has been embroidered on various <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> equipment as a mark of the brand\'s British origin,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and the Reebok Union Jack has been referred to as a brand icon.<sup id="cite_ref-upshaw_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upshaw-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Many music artists have used the Union flag ranging from rock artists <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols" title="Sex Pistols">Sex Pistols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury#Illness_and_death" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morrissey" title="Morrissey">Morrissey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard#Hysteria_era_(1984\xe2\x80\x931989)" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a>, to the pop girl group the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls#Cool_Britannia" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" London</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_India" title="Flag of India">Flag of India</a> (Flag of British India)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It has been claimed that "Union Jack" was the name given to the flag flown on the "<a href="/wiki/Jackstaff" title="Jackstaff">jack staff</a>" of ships of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, however the etymology is ultimately uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Graham Bartram (born 1963), a British vexillologist who is, as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the secretary-general for congresses of the <i>F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ration internationale des associations vexillologiques</i> and the chief vexillologist of the Flag Institute, when interviewed on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> <i>Broadcasting House</i> programme on 13 October 2013, stated that either name was perfectly valid whatever the purpose. He stated that the theory that the flag should only be referred to as "Union Jack" when flown at sea was wrong.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Jack&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20151105150921/http://www.royal.gov.uk/MonarchUK/Symbols/UnionJack.aspx">"The official website of The British Monarchy"</a>. <i>Royal.gov.uk</i>.
